### Post by rt-2 on 2010-08-05
Hi,
I'd like to have a console with a great resolution, right now,  it's about 800x600..:(

I've tried changing it but with no success.

here's my /etc/default/grub
```
# If you change this file, run 'update-grub' afterwards to update
# /boot/grub/grub.cfg.

GRUB_DEFAULT=0
GRUB_HIDDEN_TIMEOUT=0
GRUB_HIDDEN_TIMEOUT_QUIET=true
GRUB_TIMEOUT=10
GRUB_DISTRIBUTOR=`lsb_release -i -s 2> /dev/null || echo Debian`
GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT="services vga=795"
GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX=""

# Uncomment to disable graphical terminal (grub-pc only)
#GRUB_TERMINAL=console

# The resolution used on graphical terminal
# note that you can use only modes which your graphic card supports via VBE
# you can see them in real GRUB with the command `vbeinfo'
#GRUB_GFXMODE=640x480

# Uncomment if you don't want GRUB to pass "root=UUID=xxx" parameter to Linux
#GRUB_DISABLE_LINUX_UUID=true

# Uncomment to disable generation of recovery mode menu entries
#GRUB_DISABLE_LINUX_RECOVERY="true"

# Uncomment to get a beep at grub start
#GRUB_INIT_TUNE="480 440 1"
```
And my screen resolution is normaly 1600x900

Thank you

### Post by utilitytrack on 2010-08-10
Hello again. This is list of video modes that can use the framebuffer device of your video card (in according to [FONT="Courier New"]hwinfo[/FONT]):
```
[FONT="Courier New"]
  Mode 0x0300: 640x400 (+640), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0301: 640x480 (+640), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0303: 800x600 (+800), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0305: 1024x768 (+1024), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0307: 1280x1024 (+1280), 8 bits
  Mode 0x030e: 320x200 (+640), 16 bits
  Mode 0x030f: 320x200 (+1280), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0311: 640x480 (+1280), 16 bits
  Mode 0x0312: 640x480 (+2560), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0314: 800x600 (+1600), 16 bits
  Mode 0x0315: 800x600 (+3200), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0317: 1024x768 (+2048), 16 bits
  Mode 0x0318: 1024x768 (+4096), 24 bits
  Mode 0x031a: 1280x1024 (+2560), 16 bits
  Mode 0x031b: 1280x1024 (+5120), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0330: 320x200 (+320), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0331: 320x400 (+320), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0332: 320x400 (+640), 16 bits
  Mode 0x0333: 320x400 (+1280), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0334: 320x240 (+320), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0335: 320x240 (+640), 16 bits
  Mode 0x0336: 320x240 (+1280), 24 bits
  Mode 0x033d: 640x400 (+1280), 16 bits
  Mode 0x033e: 640x400 (+2560), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0345: 1600x1200 (+1600), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0346: 1600x1200 (+3200), 16 bits
  Mode 0x0347: 1400x1050 (+1400), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0348: 1400x1050 (+2800), 16 bits
  Mode 0x0349: 1400x1050 (+5600), 24 bits
  Mode 0x034a: 1600x1200 (+6400), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0352: 2048x1536 (+8192), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0360: 1280x800 (+1280), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0361: 1280x800 (+5120), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0362: 768x480 (+768), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0364: 1440x900 (+1440), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0365: 1440x900 (+5760), 24 bits
  Mode 0x0368: 1680x1050 (+1680), 8 bits
  Mode 0x0369: 1680x1050 (+6720), 24 bits
  Mode 0x037b: 1280x720 (+5120), 24 bits
  Mode 0x037c: 1920x1200 (+1920), 8 bits
  Mode 0x037d: 1920x1200 (+7680), 24 bits[/FONT]
```

Next you can use any of these modes. Simple change value of [FONT="Courier New"]vga=[/FONT] parameter that pass to kernel on boot. For example ([FONT="Courier New"]etc/default/grub[/FONT] file):
```
GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT="vga=0x0346"
```
that give you 1600x1200, 16 bits mode.

### Post by utilitytrack on 2010-08-10
Such mode as "1600x900" are not present in list above. It's mean that you can't use it. You should use some other mode instead.

See this: > [I]vga=<mode>
  <mode> here is either an integer (in C notation, either
  decimal, octal, or hexadecimal) or one of the strings
  "normal" (meaning 0xFFFF), "ext" (meaning 0xFFFE) or "ask"
  (meaning 0xFFFD).  This value should be entered into the
  vid_mode field, as it is used by the kernel before the command
  line is parsed.[/I]
source: Linux kernel documentation on [http://git.kernel.org/?p=linux/kernel/git/torvalds/linux-2.6.git;a=blob;f=Documentation/x86/boot.txt]("http://git.kernel.org/?p=linux/kernel/git/torvalds/linux-2.6.git;a=blob;f=Documentation/x86/boot.txt")

PS
Your situation has nothing to do with the one you specified in link.

### Post by utilitytrack on 2010-08-11
> *I don't understand why 1600x900 is not on my list because this is the default resolution of my screen.*

Default resolution of your screen and video modes supported by VideoBIOS of your video adapter these are things that are not related.

PS
After modification of [FONT="Courier New"]/etc/defaylt/grub[/FONT] file did you not fordet run [FONT="Courier New"]# update-grub[/FONT] command?
And post here  [FONT="Courier New"]dpkg -l | grep -E grub[/FONT]

### Post by utilitytrack on 2010-08-11
> **rt-2 said:**
> I did forget to *# update-grub* but I just did it and nothing changed.

Oh. The command [FONT="Courier New"]# update-grub[/FONT] mean [FONT="Courier New"]sudo update-grub[/FONT]. This needs to run every time after modifying [FONT="Courier New"]/etc/default/grub[/FONT] file.

### Post by utilitytrack on 2010-08-11
Ok, sorry me. Well, if as you said modifying the kernel command line is not help then we can try next following. We will use capabilities of GRUB2 bootloader.

In /etc/default/grub file:
First, pay attention on value of [FONT="Courier New"]vga=[/FONT] parameter from GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT line. For example it is [FONT="Courier New"]vga=0x0317[/FONT] i.e. 1024x768 and 16 bits of color.

Next, change the line #GRUB_GFXMODE=640x480 (uncomment it) and modify resolution according to translated [FONT="Courier New"]vga=[/FONT] parameter:
```
GRUB_GFXMODE=1024x768x16
```

If all of this will not work, probable you need use other framebuffer driver except default [FONT="Courier New"]vesafb[/FONT], for example [FONT="Courier New"]nvidiafb[/FONT]. But don't forget that nvidiafb is incompatible with the proprietary nvidia drivers (it's name [FONT="Courier New"]nvidia[/FONT])

---
